Brittney: + Get to the hill, find your place in the forest. The streams still flow free, now drink. Lap up the remanence of purity, of a nature pushed to the distance. The sound of the birds chirping, the sound of the branches swaying, the calming breeze are overcome with the roaring advance of the machines. Down below they scurry in their metropolis, bludgeoning all in their wake for financial security. Humanity has been lost, now they are dictated to only by media, stories and biased accounts of history. No one knows their own nature. No one knows that we are captive apes. We have forgotten, as long as civilization exists, we are all endangered species. And it exists, and it expands, and it engulfs, beats and oppresses all in its wake. But we refuse to succumb, we refuse to bow, to be swallowed into the bowels of the shallow and depraved, who care not for the earth and all inhabitants but only for the profits that can be made from destruction. Well, we too believe in destruction, we too believe in chaos and in acting with uncivilized intentions. We believe in the counterattack, we notice this is the last chance we will ever have to fight back. Any later and we will be caught, dragged away, shot and disappeared. Our identities will be wiped from the system, our families threatened if they dare to ask questions. Do you hear the machines? They are hauling their weight, kicking up the earth, forging a path and advancing. Soon the forest will be no more, soon there will be a new access road and an industrial park. Soon after that, people will begin to forget there was ever a forest there at all, oxygen will be replaced by fumes and it will all become accepted as every day life. Look to your left, there is a deer stood still in fear, what about her? Look to your right, there is a cowering fox with glistening wide eyes, what about him? What about the views of government, media, corporations? These are people, just like you or I, they bleed the same and they die the same.

Brittney: + We're 2 days into 2022 according to the Gregorian calendar and I feel no different. I neither do the "new year, new me" thing, nor do I do resolutions. I do themes, though. This years theme is to slow down. Slow down with what I say "yes" to at work; slow down with the plans I make for leisure, to give myself time to do the things I want. Slow down so I can be more present with my loved ones, and especially when my little one arrives. A couple days ago, I had a story prompt asking folks to reflect on an impact, memory, or moment they had with/of me in 2021 and I received some of the kindest, most genuine, tender, and insightful responses. I was genuinely moved to tears by a few (we'll blame it on hormones lol). I am someone who rarely sees myself as impactful - believe it or not, I think of myself as forgettable to most, or that I overstate my importance in their lives. I still intend to share/respond to them, but keeping with my theme, I am taking my time to honor my capacity (the booster had me down yesterday) and to be intentional: in the meantime, thank you, truly. If you read this/are seeing this - I am glad you're still here. Not on my platform, but on this plane and this timeline. I am glad to know you, in whatever way I do, and the ways you welcome getting to know me. I send my well-wishes and love to you, if you're open to receiving. A couple questions if you wanna answer: What are your hopes for 2022? What are you looking forward to? What are your worries?
